Rebbi Ḥelbo in the name of Rav Ḥuna: One divides the door into half, then into thirds, and puts it at the top of the lowest third. What is between them? The place of the <i>mezuzzah</i> is between them<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">According to Samuel, the box containing the <i>mezuzzah</i> has to be fixed so that its lower end be at ⅔ of the height of the door-post. Rav Huna divides the height of the door-post into sixths (first halves and then each half into thirds). For him the upper rim of the <i>mezuzzah</i> case has to be at the upper end of the fourth sixth, which is two thirds. Therefore the place of the lower end for Samuel is the place of the upper end for Rav Ḥuna. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 33a" href="/Menachot.33a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>33a</a>.</i>. Bar Tabari asked Rebbi Isaac, think of it, if it was a high gate? He said to him, he puts it at his shoulder’s height. The house of study of Rebbi Ḥanina was made so. Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac: the container of Rebbi’s <i>mezuzzah</i> was made like a bolt<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">It was attached horizontally, satisfying both Samuel and Rav Ḥuna. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 33a" href="/Menachot.33a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>33a</a>.</i>. If it was hung on the door, a danger and it is no meritorious deed<sup class="footnote-marker">150,</sup><i class="footnote">When Jewish worship was forbidden during the Hadrianic persecutions, changing the traditional forms of <i>tefillin</i> is not acceptable.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 32b" href="/Menachot.32b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>32b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Megillah (Lieberman) 3:30" href="/Tosefta_Megillah_(Lieberman).3.30">Tosephta 3:30</a>.</i>. If he excavated the top of a stick and put it at an unbecoming place, a danger and it is no meritorious deed<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">When Jewish worship was forbidden during the Hadrianic persecutions, changing the traditional forms of <i>tefillin</i> is not acceptable.</i>. Rebbi Abba in the name of Rav Jehudah: even if he (nailed) [did not nail] it<sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">The corrector’s addition should be deleted. Rav Jehudah disqualifies a long stick with a <i>mezuzzah</i> placed inside even if it is nailed to a door-post.</i>. But did we not state, on condition that he nailed it? Rebbi Yose said, on condition that he dedicated {the place} for it<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">Rebbi Yose accepts the stick if it truly is permanently affixed.</i>. Those of the family Malwan did so in the wars.<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">One of the uprisings against the Romans, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 5:5:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.5.5.4"><i>Yoma</i>5:7, Note 172</a>. They affixed their <i>mezuzzah</i> that it was securely attached but still easily removed in times of danger.</i> Samuel said, if it was put inside<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">Away from the outer rim of the door-post. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 33b" href="/Menachot.33b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 33b</a>.</i> more than a hand-breadth it is disqualified. Rebbi Ze`ira in the name of Samuel: It is necessary that its <i>shema`</i> see the door<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">He requires that the paragraph starting with <i>shema`</i> be written last on the sheet. The sheet then has to be rolled so that the last paragraph is on the outside.</i>. Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Ze`ira: So is the <i>baraita</i>, a doorpost serving two doors he puts it on the one he chooses. How can its <i>shema`</i> see the door<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">If there are two doors, and the <i>shema`</i> is on the side of one door, it is pointing away from the other door.</i>? If a house<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">Usually a “house” is a one-room piece. It is then stated that a one-room house needs only one <i>mezuzzah</i>; the <i>mezuzzah</i> is an obligation attached to the house, not the door.</i> has two doors, he puts it on the one usually used. If both were usually used he puts it in front. If both were in front he puts it on the one he chooses. A door which opens to the roof or to a garden is as if open to a wall, the words of Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Jehudah. But the Sages are saying, it is as open to the market<sup class="footnote-marker">201,</sup><i class="footnote">And therefore acceptable as unique <i>mezuzzah.</i> <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 33b" href="/Menachot.33b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 33b</a>.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 32b" href="/Menachot.32b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>32b</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Megillah (Lieberman) 3:30" href="/Tosefta_Megillah_(Lieberman).3.30">Tosephta 3:30</a>.</i>.
He who dwells outside the Land or dwells in a hostelry in the Land of Israel for thirty days need not put up a <i>mezuzzah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 44a" href="/Menachot.44a">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 44a</a>.</i>. Longer than that he has to put up a <i>mezuzzah</i>. He who dwells in a rural tower for thirty days has to put up a <i>mezuzzah</i>. He who rents a house from a Jew has to put up a <i>mezuzzah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">The renter is responsible to supply the <i>mezuzzah</i>. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 4a" href="/Pesachim.4a">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 4a</a>, <i>Bava meṣia`</i> 102a.</i>. He who rents a house from a Gentile has to put up a <i>mezuzzah</i>, and when he leaves he removes it, but from a Jew it is forbidden to act in this way. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Josias, because of what happened. It happened that a person removed and was burying his children. He who dwells dwells in a hostelry outside the Land of Israel for thirty days need not put up a <i>mezuzzah</i>. If he put up, he may not remove it. Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Josias, because of what happened. It happened that a person removed and was burying his children.
<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">These lines are copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 1:1:18" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.1.1.18"><i>Yoma</i> 1:1, Notes 108–111</a>.</i><i>Ḥuldat hammulim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">A direct translation would be “mole of circumcised”, which makes no sense. The explanation of <i>Qorban haEdah</i>, “entrances of cave dwellings” has no linguistic basis and would be superfluous. A possibility is Jastrow’s explanation, “loading and unloading dock for mules”, from מולא, Latin <i>mulus, mula</i>, the mule.</i> is liable for <i>mezuzah</i>. A window, four by four {cubits} wide, in which slaves sit and make wind for their masters are liable for <i>mezuzah</i>. Coops one on top of the other are liable for <i>mezuzah</i>; one steps on the doorstep below<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">If the chicken coops are part of the house and are directly accessible from the doorstep, and the areas of the openings add up to four-by-four cubits.</i>. Rebbi Yose was sorry not to have seen the coop of Rebbi Ilai which he had made according to all rabbis<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">That it was required to have a <i>mezuzah</i> according to everybody.</i>.
<i>Tefillin</i> and <i>mezuzzah</i>, which one has precedence? Samuel said, <i>mezuzzah</i> has precedence. Rav Ḥuna said, <i>tefillin</i> have precedence. What is Samuel’s reason? Since it applies on holidays and Sabbath<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">Whereas <i>tefillin</i> are strictly only worn on working days.</i>. What is Rav Ḥuna’s reason? Since it applies to travellers on the Seas and those who cross deserts. A <i>baraita</i><sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Soferim</i> 14:20.</i> supports Samuel: “A worn-out <i>tefillah</i> one may make into <i>mezuzzah</i>, a worn out <i>mezuzzah</i> one may not make into a <i>tefillah</i>. Why? Because one increases in holiness but may not decrease.”
